###
Yes, 1009 is a prime number.
###
To determine if 1009 is a prime number, we can check for divisibility by all numbers less than its square root.

First, find the square root of 1009: 
√1009 ≈ 31.747.

Next, check if 1009 is divisible by any prime numbers less than or equal to its square root (31.747).

Starting with 2, we divide 1009 by integers up to 31: 
1009 ÷ 2 = 504.5 (not divisible)
1009 ÷ 3 = 336.333 (not divisible)
...
1009 ÷ 29 = 34.862 (not divisible)
1009 ÷ 31 = 32.677 (not divisible)

Since 1009 is not divisible by any prime numbers less than or equal to its square root, we can conclude that 1009 is a prime number.
###
No, 1009 is not a composite number. It is a prime number.
###
A composite number is defined as a positive integer greater than 1 that has factors other than 1 and itself. 

To determine if 1009 is a composite number, we need to check if it has any factors other than 1 and 1009. 

First, we can try dividing 1009 by prime numbers starting from 2, since any composite number can be expressed as a product of prime factors. 

When we try dividing 1009 by 2, we get a quotient of 504 with a remainder of 1. 

Continuing with prime numbers, when we try dividing 1009 by 3, 5, 7, 11, and so on, we still get remainders other than 0. 

Since we have checked all the prime numbers up to the square root of 1009 (which is approximately 31.8), and there are no factors other than 1 and 1009, we can conclude that 1009 is not divisible by any integer other than 1 and itself. 

Therefore, 1009 is a prime number, not a composite number.

###
To determine if 1093 is a prime number, we can use the process of trial division. We need to test if there are any prime numbers that divide 1093 evenly.

First, we can check if 2 divides 1093. Since 1093 is an odd number and not divisible by 2, we can move on.

Next, we can check if 3 divides 1093. Adding the individual digits of 1093 (1 + 0 + 9 + 3), we get 13. Since 13 is not divisible by 3, we can also move on.

We continue this process, testing if any prime numbers larger than 3 divide 1093.

Next, we can check if 5 divides 1093. Since 1093 does not end in 5 or 0, it is not divisible by 5.

Next, we can check if 7 divides 1093. By subtracting twice the unit's digit (3 x 2) from the remaining tens and hundreds digits (109 - 6), we get 97. Since 97 is not divisible by 7, we can continue.

We continue with this process for the prime numbers up to the square root of 1093, which is approximately 33.04.

Next, we test if 11 divides 1093. By alternatingly adding and subtracting each digit, we get 9 - 3 + 1 = 7. Since 7 is not divisible by 11, we can continue.

We skip 13 since it is already higher than the square root of 1093.

Next, we test if 17 divides 1093. By doubling the unit's digit (3 x 2) and subtracting it from the tens and hundreds digits (109 - 6), we get 97. Since 97 is not divisible by 17, we can continue.

Similarly, we skip 19 and 23 since they are already greater than the square root of 1093.

Finally, we can check if 29 divides 1093. By subtracting twice the unit's digit (3 x 2) from the remaining tens and hundreds digits (109 - 6), we get 97. Since 97 is not divisible by 29, we can conclude that 1093 is not divisible by any prime numbers up to its square root.

Therefore, we can conclude that 1093 is a prime number.

So, yes, 1093 is a prime number.

To do this, we can start by checking if 2539 is divisible by any prime numbers less than or equal to the square root of 2539.

The square root of 2539 is approximately 50.386.

Let's check if 2539 is divisible by prime numbers less than or equal to 50:

2: 2539 ÷ 2 = 1269.5 (not an integer)
3: 2539 ÷ 3 = 846.3333 (not an integer)
5: 2539 ÷ 5 = 507.8 (not an integer)
7: 2539 ÷ 7 = 362.7143 (not an integer)
11: 2539 ÷ 11 = 230.8182 (not an integer)
13: 2539 ÷ 13 = 195.3077 (not an integer)
17: 2539 ÷ 17 = 149.3529 (not an integer)
19: 2539 ÷ 19 = 133.6316 (not an integer)
23: 2539 ÷ 23 = 110.3913 (not an integer)
29: 2539 ÷ 29 = 87.5517 (not an integer)
31: 2539 ÷ 31 = 81.9032 (not an integer)
37: 2539 ÷ 37 = 68.8378 (not an integer)
41: 2539 ÷ 41 = 61.9268 (not an integer)
43: 2539 ÷ 43 = 59.0233 (not an integer)
47: 2539 ÷ 47 = 54.0426 (not an integer)
49: 2539 ÷ 49 = 51.897 (not an integer)

Since 2539 is not divisible by any prime numbers less than or equal to 50, we can conclude that 2539 is a prime number.

So, yes, 2539 is a prime number.

To determine if 2557 is a prime number, we can check for divisibility using divisibility tests.

1. First, we check if 2557 is divisible by 2. A number is divisible by 2 if the last digit is even (divisible by 2). However, the last digit of 2557 is 7, which is odd. Therefore, 2557 is not divisible by 2.

2. Next, we check if 2557 is divisible by 3. A number is divisible by 3 if the sum of its digits is divisible by 3. Adding the digits of 2557, we get 2 + 5 + 5 + 7 = 19. Since 19 is not divisible by 3, 2557 is not divisible by 3.

3. Now, we check if 2557 is divisible by 5. A number is divisible by 5 if the last digit is 0 or 5. As mentioned earlier, the last digit of 2557 is 7, which is not divisible by 5. Therefore, 2557 is not divisible by 5.

4. We can continue checking divisibility by other prime numbers, but let's move on to a faster approach called the square root test. 

Using the square root test, we only need to check divisibility up to the square root of 2557, which is approximately 50.57 (rounded up to 51).

By checking divisibility of 2557 by all prime numbers less than or equal to 51, we can conclude that 2557 is indeed a prime number.

Therefore, 2557 is a prime number.
